The First Meaning of Time: Concomitance of Renewing Things
Sanusi defines the first meaning of time and proves its impossibility for Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's first definition of time as a relation between two originated events and why it cannot apply to Allah.

Core Idea
Time as a relation between two originated things has no place in pre-eternity.

Sanusi begins by establishing that time is a property of contingent beings. He then presents the first meaning of time as the concomitance of one renewing thing to another. This definition immediately shows why time cannot be attributed to Allah, as renewal is impossible for Him.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the first meaning of time
Read the Arabic and translation, focusing on the definition of time as 'concomitance of one renewing thing to another'. Note the example of travel and sunrise.
This is a relation between two originated events.
2
Understand why a relation depends on two existing things
Sanusi argues that the relation (time) exists only after the two related things exist. Understand the logical dependency.
The relation is contingent upon its relata.
3
Apply the argument to Allah
Since there is no renewing thing in pre-eternity (al-azal), time cannot exist. Renewal is impossible for Allah, so time cannot be attributed to Him.
This applies to both pre-eternity and perpetuity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
زمانيّاً ، ولا نسبةَ للزمان إلى وجودِهِ ألبتة ؛ إذ هو مِنْ صفاتِ المحدَثِ ، فيكونُ حادثاً ضرورةً ؛ فإنَّ الزمان إمَّا عبارة عن مقارنة متجدّدٍ لمتجدّدٍ ؛ أي : حادث لحادث ؛ كمقارنة السفر لطلوع الشمس مثلاً ، فثبوته فرع وجودِ حادثين مقترني الوجودِ ؛ لأنَّهُ نسبةُ بينَهما ، والنسبةُ يتأخر وجودها عن وجودِ المنتسبين ، ولا متجدِّدَ في الأزلِ ، فلا زمانَ ، والتجدُّدُ لوجودِهِ جلَّ وعلا وصفاتِ ذاتِهِ العليَّةِ . . محالٌ ، فنسبة الزمان إليه تعالى محال على الإطلاق ، في الأزلِ وفيما لا يزالُ وإما عبارة عن حركاتِ الأفلاكِ ، وما يرجع إليها مِنَ الساعاتِ وأجزائها ، وتعاقب الليل والنهار : إذ الليل : عبارة عن مغيب الشمس تحت الأفق ، والنهارُ : عبارةٌ عن ظهورها فوق الأفق ، وذلك في الحقيقة عبارة عن سير الفَلَكِ الأعظم مُعدَّل النهارِ بها تحت الأفق أو فوقه على ما تزعم الفلاسفة ، والساعةُ : عبارةٌ عن سيرِ مُعدَّل النهارِ خمسَ عشرةَ درجةً ؛ أي: خمسةَ عشرَ قِسْماً مِنْ ثلاث مئة وستينَ قسماً متساوية قسموا الفلك بها اصطلاحاً ، والزمانُ بهذا المعنى هو الموجود كثيراً في تعارفِ أهل العاداتِ ، ولا شك في انعدام الزمانِ بهذا المعنى أيضاً في الأزلِ ؛ إذْ لا فَلَكَ فيهِ ولا حركة ؛ لما عرفت مِنْ برهان حدوثِ كلٌّ ما سوى اللهِ جَلَّ وعلا ويستحيلُ أنْ يمرَّ عليهِ جلَّ وعلا الزمانُ بهذا المعنى ؛ لأنَّهُ إِنَّما يمرُّ على الأفلاكِ وما أحاطَتْ بهِ ممَّا سُجِنَ في جوفها ، حتى تمر عليه الأزمنةُ مِنَ الساعاتِ والليل والنهار وفصول السنة وأشهرها بحسَبِ تحرُّكِ الأفلاكِ فوقه وتحته ، وظهور الشمس وارتفاعها فوق الأُفُقِ وغَيبتها وانخفاضها تحت الأفقِ ؛ لتتقيّد بذلك أعراضُهُ المتجدّدةُ ; مِنْ يقظة ونوم، وصحة وسقم ، وحياةٍ وموتٍ ، ونحو ذلك ، وتتقيّد معايشُهُ المقدَّرة خريفاً وصيفاً وربيعاً وشتاءً بتدبيرِ مَنْ ليس كمثلِهِ شيء ، لا إله إلا هو ربُّ كلِّ شيءٍ تبارك وتعالى ، ومَنْ تنزَّهَ أَنْ تحيط به الأمكنة ، أو تتجدد أو تتغيَّرَ لهُ صفةٌ .. كيف يتصوَّرُ أنْ يكونَ لهُ معَ شيءٍ مِنَ العالم اتصال أو انفصال ؟! فقد اتضحَ لكَ : أنَّ الزمانَ على كلا الاعتبارينِ إِنَّما هو مِنْ صفاتِ الحوادثِ ، ولا يتقيَّدُ به إلا ما هو حادث ، فالقدم إذاً باعتباره خاص بالحوادث
Temporally, and there is no relation of time to His existence at all; because it is among the attributes of the contingent being, so it would necessarily be originated. For time is either an expression of the concomitance of one renewing thing to another renewing thing, i.e., an originated [thing] to an originated [thing], like the concomitance of travel to sunrise for example; so its establishment is a branch of the existence of two originated things whose existence is concurrent, because it is a relation between them, and the relation's existence is delayed from the existence of the two related things. And there is no renewing thing in pre-eternity (al-azal), so there is no time. Renewal for His existence, may He be exalted and magnified, and the attributes of His high essence is impossible. So the attribution of time to Him, the Exalted, is absolutely impossible, in pre-eternity and in perpetuity. Or it is an expression of the movements of the celestial spheres, and what returns to them of hours and their parts, and the succession of night and day: for night is an expression of the sun's setting below the horizon, and day is an expression of its appearance above the horizon; that is in reality an expression of the motion of the greatest sphere, the celestial equator, below the horizon or above it according to the philosophers claim. And the hour is an expression of the motion of the celestial equator through fifteen degrees, i.e., fifteen parts out of three hundred and sixty equal parts by which they divided the sphere conventionally. Time in this sense is what is found frequently in the custom of people of habits. And there is no doubt in the non-existence of time in this sense as well in pre-eternity (al-azal), since there is no sphere therein nor motion, due to what you have known of the proof of the origination of everything other than Allah, may He be exalted and magnified. And it is impossible that time in this sense passes over Him, may He be exalted and magnified, because it only passes over the celestial spheres and what surrounds them of what is imprisoned in their interior, until the times of hours, night and day, seasons of the year and its months pass over it according to the movement of the spheres above and below it, and the appearance of the sun and its rising above the horizon, its setting and its descent below the horizon, so that its renewing accidents are thereby determined, from wakefulness and sleep, health and illness, life and death, and the like; and its apportioned livelihoods are determined, autumn, summer, spring and winter, by the arrangement of the One Whom nothing is like, there is no god but He, the Lord of everything, blessed and exalted. And He is elevated beyond being encompassed by places, or a description renewed or changing for Him. How can it be imagined that He has connection or disconnection with anything of the world? So it has become clear to you that time, according to both considerations, is only among the attributes of events, and only what is originated is determined by it. Pre-eternity (al-qidam) therefore, by that consideration, is specific to events.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage is a proof by classification and refutation. Sanusi argues that time cannot be attributed to Allah because time is a property of originated things. He begins by stating that time has no relation to Allah's existence at all, because it is among the attributes of the contingent (al-muhdath), and if it were attributed to Allah, He would be originated necessarily. He then classifies time into two meanings: (1) Time as the concomitance of one renewing thing to another, i.e., a relation between two originated things. He explains that such a relation exists only after the existence of the two related things, and since there is no renewing thing in pre-eternity (al-azal), there is no time. Renewal is impossible for Allah and His attributes, so attributing time to Him is absolutely impossible in pre-eternity and perpetuity. (2) Time as the movements of celestial spheres, hours, night and day. He defines night as the sun's setting below the horizon and day as its appearance above, which is really the motion of the celestial equator. Hours are defined as 1/360th of that motion. This kind of time is commonly used. But it does not exist in pre-eternity because there was no sphere or motion, as proven by the proof of the origination of everything other than Allah. Furthermore, it is impossible for such time to pass over Allah, because it only passes over the spheres and what is within them, determining their renewing accidents (like sleep, health, life) and seasonal livelihoods. Allah is utterly transcendent beyond places, renewal, or change. Sanusi then concludes that time in both senses is only a property of events, and only originated things are determined by it. Therefore, the term 'pre-eternity' (al-qidam) in this sense is specific to events (i.e., time is not a property of Allah).

Key Terms
زمان
أزل
حادث
نسبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that time is a single continuous entity that applies to everything, including Allah.
Correction: Sanusi shows that time in this first meaning is a relation between two originated events, so it cannot apply to the eternal Creator who has no renewal.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, why is it impossible for time to apply to Allah in the first meaning (concomitance of two renewing things)?
A) Because time is a substance and Allah is not a substance.
B) Because there is no renewing thing in pre-eternity, and time is a relation between two originated things.
C) Because time is only a mental concept.
D) Because Allah is beyond space and time.

Key Takeaway
Time as a relation between two originated events cannot apply to Allah because there is no renewal in His essence and no originated events in pre-eternity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You live your entire life measured by time—birthdays, deadlines, prayers. If time is merely a relation between originated things, and you are one of those originated things, how does that reframe your sense of urgency and priority? What would it mean to orient your heart toward the Timeless One instead of being consumed by moments?
?
Sanusi proves that renewal is impossible for Allah. Yet you experience constant change: mood swings, spiritual highs and lows, shifting intentions. If your relationship with Allah is based on a God who does not change, then who is truly unstable—you or Him? What does that demand of you today?
?
In pre-eternity, there was no time. Your existence began at a point in time and will end at a point in time. Between those two points, you are given a sliver of time to know the One who is beyond time. If you truly believed this, what would you do differently with the next hour?

The Second Meaning of Time: Celestial Movements and Its Impossibility for Allah
Sanusi defines the second meaning of time and proves its impossibility for Allah, concluding that time is a property of events.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second definition of time as celestial motions and why Allah is beyond such temporal determinations.

Core Idea
Time as celestial motion only applies to the created universe, not to the Creator.

Sanusi now presents the second, more familiar meaning of time as the movements of the spheres, the cycle of night and day, and the hours. He demonstrates that even this time is absent in pre-eternity and cannot pass over Allah, who is free from all change.

Guided Path
1
Identify the second definition of time
Read the passage and find the second meaning: time as the movements of celestial spheres, hours, night and day. Understand that this is the conventional understanding.
Sanusi defines night and day in terms of the sun's position relative to the horizon.
2
Understand why this time did not exist in pre-eternity
Sanusi says that in pre-eternity there were no spheres or motion, as proven by the proof of origination of everything other than Allah.
This time is contingent on the existence of the universe.
3
See why this time cannot pass over Allah
Time in this sense only passes over the spheres and what is within them, determining their changing states (e.g., sleep, health, seasons). Allah is beyond place, change, and connection with the world.
The passage uses a rhetorical question: How can He have connection or disconnection with anything?
4
Conclude that time is a property of events
Sanusi concludes that both meanings of time are attributes of originated things, and only originated things are determined by time. Pre-eternity (al-qidam) in this sense is specific to events—i.e., time itself is originated.
This reinforces that Allah is timeless.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
زمانيّاً ، ولا نسبةَ للزمان إلى وجودِهِ ألبتة ؛ إذ هو مِنْ صفاتِ المحدَثِ ، فيكونُ حادثاً ضرورةً ؛ فإنَّ الزمان إمَّا عبارة عن مقارنة متجدّدٍ لمتجدّدٍ ؛ أي : حادث لحادث ؛ كمقارنة السفر لطلوع الشمس مثلاً ، فثبوته فرع وجودِ حادثين مقترني الوجودِ ؛ لأنَّهُ نسبةُ بينَهما ، والنسبةُ يتأخر وجودها عن وجودِ المنتسبين ، ولا متجدِّدَ في الأزلِ ، فلا زمانَ ، والتجدُّدُ لوجودِهِ جلَّ وعلا وصفاتِ ذاتِهِ العليَّةِ . . محالٌ ، فنسبة الزمان إليه تعالى محال على الإطلاق ، في الأزلِ وفيما لا يزالُ وإما عبارة عن حركاتِ الأفلاكِ ، وما يرجع إليها مِنَ الساعاتِ وأجزائها ، وتعاقب الليل والنهار : إذ الليل : عبارة عن مغيب الشمس تحت الأفق ، والنهارُ : عبارةٌ عن ظهورها فوق الأفق ، وذلك في الحقيقة عبارة عن سير الفَلَكِ الأعظم مُعدَّل النهارِ بها تحت الأفق أو فوقه على ما تزعم الفلاسفة ، والساعةُ : عبارةٌ عن سيرِ مُعدَّل النهارِ خمسَ عشرةَ درجةً ؛ أي: خمسةَ عشرَ قِسْماً مِنْ ثلاث مئة وستينَ قسماً متساوية قسموا الفلك بها اصطلاحاً ، والزمانُ بهذا المعنى هو الموجود كثيراً في تعارفِ أهل العاداتِ ، ولا شك في انعدام الزمانِ بهذا المعنى أيضاً في الأزلِ ؛ إذْ لا فَلَكَ فيهِ ولا حركة ؛ لما عرفت مِنْ برهان حدوثِ كلٌّ ما سوى اللهِ جَلَّ وعلا ويستحيلُ أنْ يمرَّ عليهِ جلَّ وعلا الزمانُ بهذا المعنى ؛ لأنَّهُ إِنَّما يمرُّ على الأفلاكِ وما أحاطَتْ بهِ ممَّا سُجِنَ في جوفها ، حتى تمر عليه الأزمنةُ مِنَ الساعاتِ والليل والنهار وفصول السنة وأشهرها بحسَبِ تحرُّكِ الأفلاكِ فوقه وتحته ، وظهور الشمس وارتفاعها فوق الأُفُقِ وغَيبتها وانخفاضها تحت الأفقِ ؛ لتتقيّد بذلك أعراضُهُ المتجدّدةُ ; مِنْ يقظة ونوم، وصحة وسقم ، وحياةٍ وموتٍ ، ونحو ذلك ، وتتقيّد معايشُهُ المقدَّرة خريفاً وصيفاً وربيعاً وشتاءً بتدبيرِ مَنْ ليس كمثلِهِ شيء ، لا إله إلا هو ربُّ كلِّ شيءٍ تبارك وتعالى ، ومَنْ تنزَّهَ أَنْ تحيط به الأمكنة ، أو تتجدد أو تتغيَّرَ لهُ صفةٌ .. كيف يتصوَّرُ أنْ يكونَ لهُ معَ شيءٍ مِنَ العالم اتصال أو انفصال ؟! فقد اتضحَ لكَ : أنَّ الزمانَ على كلا الاعتبارينِ إِنَّما هو مِنْ صفاتِ الحوادثِ ، ولا يتقيَّدُ به إلا ما هو حادث ، فالقدم إذاً باعتباره خاص بالحوادث
Temporally, and there is no relation of time to His existence at all; because it is among the attributes of the contingent being, so it would necessarily be originated. For time is either an expression of the concomitance of one renewing thing to another renewing thing, i.e., an originated [thing] to an originated [thing], like the concomitance of travel to sunrise for example; so its establishment is a branch of the existence of two originated things whose existence is concurrent, because it is a relation between them, and the relation's existence is delayed from the existence of the two related things. And there is no renewing thing in pre-eternity (al-azal), so there is no time. Renewal for His existence, may He be exalted and magnified, and the attributes of His high essence is impossible. So the attribution of time to Him, the Exalted, is absolutely impossible, in pre-eternity and in perpetuity. Or it is an expression of the movements of the celestial spheres, and what returns to them of hours and their parts, and the succession of night and day: for night is an expression of the sun's setting below the horizon, and day is an expression of its appearance above the horizon; that is in reality an expression of the motion of the greatest sphere, the celestial equator, below the horizon or above it according to the philosophers claim. And the hour is an expression of the motion of the celestial equator through fifteen degrees, i.e., fifteen parts out of three hundred and sixty equal parts by which they divided the sphere conventionally. Time in this sense is what is found frequently in the custom of people of habits. And there is no doubt in the non-existence of time in this sense as well in pre-eternity (al-azal), since there is no sphere therein nor motion, due to what you have known of the proof of the origination of everything other than Allah, may He be exalted and magnified. And it is impossible that time in this sense passes over Him, may He be exalted and magnified, because it only passes over the celestial spheres and what surrounds them of what is imprisoned in their interior, until the times of hours, night and day, seasons of the year and its months pass over it according to the movement of the spheres above and below it, and the appearance of the sun and its rising above the horizon, its setting and its descent below the horizon, so that its renewing accidents are thereby determined, from wakefulness and sleep, health and illness, life and death, and the like; and its apportioned livelihoods are determined, autumn, summer, spring and winter, by the arrangement of the One Whom nothing is like, there is no god but He, the Lord of everything, blessed and exalted. And He is elevated beyond being encompassed by places, or a description renewed or changing for Him. How can it be imagined that He has connection or disconnection with anything of the world? So it has become clear to you that time, according to both considerations, is only among the attributes of events, and only what is originated is determined by it. Pre-eternity (al-qidam) therefore, by that consideration, is specific to events.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage is a proof by classification and refutation. Sanusi argues that time cannot be attributed to Allah because time is a property of originated things. He begins by stating that time has no relation to Allah's existence at all, because it is among the attributes of the contingent (al-muhdath), and if it were attributed to Allah, He would be originated necessarily. He then classifies time into two meanings: (1) Time as the concomitance of one renewing thing to another, i.e., a relation between two originated things. He explains that such a relation exists only after the existence of the two related things, and since there is no renewing thing in pre-eternity (al-azal), there is no time. Renewal is impossible for Allah and His attributes, so attributing time to Him is absolutely impossible in pre-eternity and perpetuity. (2) Time as the movements of celestial spheres, hours, night and day. He defines night as the sun's setting below the horizon and day as its appearance above, which is really the motion of the celestial equator. Hours are defined as 1/360th of that motion. This kind of time is commonly used. But it does not exist in pre-eternity because there was no sphere or motion, as proven by the proof of the origination of everything other than Allah. Furthermore, it is impossible for such time to pass over Allah, because it only passes over the spheres and what is within them, determining their renewing accidents (like sleep, health, life) and seasonal livelihoods. Allah is utterly transcendent beyond places, renewal, or change. Sanusi then concludes that time in both senses is only a property of events, and only originated things are determined by it. Therefore, the term 'pre-eternity' (al-qidam) in this sense is specific to events (i.e., time is not a property of Allah).

زمان
أزل
فلك
ساعة
ليل
نهار
حركة

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the common understanding of time as day and night or the motion of the sun applies to Allah's existence.
Correction: Sanusi shows that such time depends on celestial motion, which began with creation, and only applies to changing things. Allah is unchanging and beyond such temporal determinations.

Checkpoint

B) Because there were no spheres or motion in pre-eternity, as everything other than Allah is originated.
C) Because the sun did not exist.
D) Because Allah created time later.

Key Takeaway
Time as celestial motion is a property of the created world; Allah is utterly transcendent and timeless.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

You measure your life in hours and days. But this lesson says time is only a property of created events. ?
The passage says time determines 'your renewing accidents'—wakefulness, health, life itself. When you worry about aging or the future, are you trusting in the Timeless One or are you imprisoned by the very time that He created? How can you surrender your timeline to Him today?
?
Sanusi asks: 'How can it be imagined that He has connection or disconnection with anything of the world?' Reflect on a recent moment when you felt Allah was 'distant' or 'close' due to time—perhaps after a long wait or a sudden event. Does this lesson challenge that feeling? What does it mean to relate to a Being who is utterly beyond time?

Pre-eternity Necessitates Eternal Continuance
Sanusi presents a concise definitive proof that pre-eternity implies eternal continuance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof that God's pre-eternity entails His eternal continuance and the universal rule derived from it.

Core Idea
If something is pre-eternal by necessity, it cannot cease to exist.

In this passage, Sanusi presents a compact yet definitive argument linking two essential divine attributes: pre-eternity (qidam) and eternal continuance (baqa'). The proof is remarkable for its brevity and logical force. As you read, pay attention to how the author moves from a rhetorical question to a universal rule, and how each step builds on the previous one.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic source text once, then read the literal translation. Notice the rhetorical question at the beginning and the confident tone.
The Arabic uses a question to assert a point—a common kalam technique.
2
Trace the logical steps
Identify the premises: (1) pre-eternity is proven, (2) pre-eternity necessitates eternal continuance, (3) allowing later non-existence would imply prior non-existence, which contradicts pre-eternity.
The proof is a brief syllogism; see how the conclusion is drawn.
3
Understand the universal rule
Sanusi extracts a universal rule: anything whose pre-eternity is established cannot cease to exist. Reflect on why this rule holds for God alone.
This rule applies only to the Necessary Being.
4
Reflect on the proof's certainty
Sanusi asserts that the proof is definitive and its premises are free from doubt. Consider why he emphasizes this point.
Certainty in proofs is crucial in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كيف وقد ثبت بالبرهان القطعي وجوبُ قدمِهِ؟! وجوب القدم يستلزم وجوب البقاء فبانَ لكَ بهذا البرهانِ: أَنَّ وجوبَ القدم يستلزم أبداً وجوبَ البقاء، وأنَّ تجويز العدم اللاحقِ يُوجِبُ ثبوت العدم السابقِ، فخرج لنا بهذا البرهان قاعدة كليةٌ؛ وهي: أَنَّ كلَّ ما ثبَتَ قدمُهُ استحالَ عدمه؛ لأنَّ القدم لا يكون أبداً إلا واجباً للقديم. وهذا البرهانُ الذي ذكرنا لوجوبِ البقاء مختصر، وهو معَ اختصارِهِ قطعي لا شبهة في شيءٍ مِنْ مُقدِّماتِه.
How, when it has been established by the definitive proof the necessity of His pre-eternity?! The necessity of pre-eternity entails the necessity of eternal continuance. So it became clear to you by this proof: that the necessity of pre-eternity always entails the necessity of eternal continuance, and that allowing subsequent non-existence necessitates establishing prior non-existence. So there emerged for us from this proof a universal rule: that everything whose pre-eternity is established, its non-existence is impossible, because pre-eternity is never except as necessary for the Pre-eternal. And this proof which we have mentioned for the necessity of eternal continuance is concise, and despite its conciseness it is definitive, there is no obscurity in any of its premises.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage presents a concise proof for the necessary eternal continuance (wujub al-baqa') of God. It begins with a rhetorical question emphasizing that God's pre-eternity (qidam) is established by definitive proof. The argument follows: necessity of pre-eternity entails necessity of persistence; if subsequent non-existence were possible, it would imply prior non-existence, contradicting pre-eternity. From this, a universal rule is extracted: whatever is necessarily pre-eternal cannot cease to exist. The author then notes that this proof, despite its brevity, is certain and its premises are sound.

Key Terms

وجوب البقاء
العدم اللاحق
العدم السابق
قاعدة كلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think pre-eternity does not necessarily mean a being cannot cease to exist later.
Correction: The proof shows that if a being is pre-eternal by necessity, allowing later non-existence would imply prior non-existence, which is contradictory. Hence pre-eternity necessitates eternal continuance.

Checkpoint

B) necessity of eternal continuance (wujub al-baqa')
C) impossibility of existence
D) creation in time

Key Takeaway
God's pre-eternity logically entails His eternal continuance; a pre-eternal being cannot cease to exist.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

If God's pre-eternity necessarily implies that He will always exist, what does that mean for your own sense of permanence? Do you live as though God is the only permanent reality? What would change if you truly internalized that everything else is contingent and will pass away?
?
The proof shows that allowing non-existence for God would contradict pre-eternity. Are there areas in your life where you act as if God's attributes are not absolute, as if He might change or fail? How can you reinforce your certainty in His eternal power?
?
Since pre-eternity and eternal continuance are logically tied, consider your own mortality. How does knowing that God alone is permanent shape your priorities and your attachment to this world? What concrete step can you take today to align your life with the reality that only God remains?

Critique of the Popular Proof for God's Eternal Continuance
Sanusi recounts and critiques the longer popular proof for God's necessary eternal continuance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the longer popular proof for God's eternal continuance is considered flawed, and how each division of the argument leads to impossibility.

Core Idea
The popular proof's many branches unveil their own absurdities.

The mutakallimun commonly used a lengthy proof to argue that God must be eternal without beginning. But Sanusi shows that this proof, with its many divisions, ultimately collapses under its own weight. By breaking down the argument, we see that each possible path for explaining non-existence in the Pre-eternal leads to a logical dead end. This lesson walks through that critique.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation to get the flow of the argument. Note that it presents a proof then critiques it by examining each branch.
2
Identify the main claim
The proof claims that if non-existence occurred to the Pre-eternal, it would need a determinant. Find that starting point.
3
Follow the divisions
The passage divides the determinant into free choice or non-choice, and further divides non-choice into absence of condition or occurrence of an opposite. Trace each branch.
Notice how each leads to an impossibility.
4
Understand the critique
Sanusi argues that none of these branches can explain non-existence of the Pre-eternal, thus the proof fails. Recognize the absurdities: infinite regress, combination of opposites, etc.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والدليلُ المشهور بينَ المتكلمينَ فيهِ طول وتقسيم لم يُجمع على بطلان أقسامه؛ وذلك أنَّهم يقولون (1): لو طراً العدم على القديم لوجب أن يكونَ لهُ مقتض؛ إذْ طروقُ أمرِ لنفسِهِ بغيرِ مقتض — لا سيما إنْ كانَ مرجوحاً كهذا — محال ضرورةً، والمقتضي: إمَّا بالاختيار أو لا، والمقتضي المختار: لا يفعلُ العدمَ؛ إذْ ليسَ بفعل، وغيرُ المختارِ: إِمَّا عدمُ شرط، أو طريان ضد: وباطل أن يكونَ عدم شرط؛ لأنَّ ذلك الشرط إن كان قديماً نقلنا الكلام إلى عدمِهِ، ولزامَ التسلسل، وإنْ كانَ حادثاً لزم وجود القديم في الأزلِ بدونِ شرطِهِ، محال وهو وباطل أنْ يكونَ طريان ضد؛ لأنَّهُ إِنْ طراً قبلَ انعدام القديمِ لزمَ اجتماع الضدين، وإن طراً بعد انعدامه فقد انعدم القديم بغيرِ مقتض؛ لاستحالة تأخر المقتضي عن أثره، وأيضاً يلزم في الضد ترجيح المرجوح، ولا أقلَّ مِنَ المساوي؛ إذ دفع القديم السابق وجوده لطريان ضدّه أولى مِنَ العكس، وأيضاً فالضدُّ إِنْ قامَ بالقديم لزمَ اجتماع الضدَّينِ، وإلا بطل اقتضاؤُهُ؛ لعدم الاختصاص
And the well-known proof among the mutakallimun has length and division that does not guarantee the invalidity of its divisions. That is because they say: If non-existence were to occur to the Pre-eternal, it would necessarily have a determinant, because an occurrence of something by itself without a determinant—especially if it is unlikely like this—is impossible necessarily. The determinant is either a free choice or not. The freely choosing determinant does not bring about non-existence, because it is not an act. And the non-choosing determinant is either the absence of a condition or the occurrence of an opposite. It is invalid that it be the absence of a condition, because if that condition is pre-eternal, we transfer the discussion to its non-existence, necessitating infinite regress; and if it is originated, it would necessitate the existence of the Pre-eternal in pre-eternity without its condition, which is impossible. And it is invalid that it be the occurrence of an opposite, because if it occurs before the annihilation of the Pre-eternal, it would necessitate the combination of opposites; and if it occurs after its annihilation, then the Pre-eternal would have been annihilated without a determinant, due to the impossibility of the determinant lagging behind its effect. Also, regarding the opposite, there would be a preference of the unlikely over the likely, or at least equality, since repelling the Pre-eternal whose existence preceded [the opposite] upon the occurrence of its opposite is more likely than the reverse. And also, if the opposite inheres in the Pre-eternal, it would necessitate the combination of opposites; otherwise its causality would be invalid due to lack of specification.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage critiques the longer, divisional proof used by many mutakallimun to establish God's eternal continuance. The author notes that this proof is lengthy and its divisions are not universally agreed upon as invalid. He then recounts the argument: if non-existence were to occur to the Pre-eternal, it would need a determinant. The determinant is either voluntary or involuntary. Involuntary determinants are further divided into absence of condition or occurrence of an opposite. Each leads to absurdities: infinite regress, combination of opposites, or the determinant occurring after the effect. The author uses this to show that the concise proof is superior.

Key Terms
دليل مشهور
مقتض
اختيار
عدم شرط
طريان ضد
تسلسل
اجتماع الضدين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The popular proof is sound because it is widely used by mutakallimun.
Correction: Sanusi demonstrates that the proof's own divisions lead to logical contradictions, showing it is not a valid proof.

Checkpoint
What does the popular proof consider as possible determinants for the non-existence of the Pre-eternal?
A) free choice and non-choice
B) only free choice
C) only non-choice
D) direct action

Key Takeaway
The popular proof for God's eternal continuance, despite its thoroughness in division, fails because all its branches lead to logical contradictions such as infinite regress or combination of opposites.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever accepted a popular argument about Allah without critically examining its logical consistency? What might that reveal about the strength of your convictions, and are you willing to test them against the rigorous standards of 'ilm al-kalam?
?
The popular proof leads to absurdities like infinite regress. Are there any beliefs you hold about Allah that, upon deeper reflection, might imply contradictions? Will you seek to resolve them even if it means abandoning comfortable positions?
?
The author shows that free will cannot produce non-existence. How does this affect your understanding of Allah's actions? Does it challenge any assumptions you had about the relationship between Allah's will and the existence or non-existence of things? Commit to revisiting your mental model of divine causality before this day ends.

Proof That Accidents Do Not Endure
Sanusi presents the Ash'ari proof for the impossibility of accidents enduring.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari argument that accidents are constantly recreated and do not endure, and how they respond to the objection about substances.

Core Idea
Accidents are re-created each moment; only God's continuous creation sustains them.

This lesson presents the Ash'ari proof that accidents (a'rad) have no endurance. The argument builds on a similar proof for God's eternal existence. It also addresses a key objection regarding substances (jawahir) and explains that substances endure only through God's continuous bestowal of accidents.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Sanusi uses a very compressed style here.
2
Identify the proof, objection, and answer
The passage has three parts: the proof that accidents do not endure, an objection from the endurance of substances, and the answer that substances endure only because of continuous creation of accidents. Find each part and see how they connect.
3
Reflect on the theological significance
Consider why this matters: if accidents endured, they could not cease, but we observe them ceasing. The answer shows that all created things depend on God's ongoing creative act.
This connects to the Ash'ari doctrine of occasionalism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم: أنَّ بمثل هذا البرهان استدلَّ أئمَّةُ السنَّةِ رضي الله عنهم على استحالة بقاء الأعراض. قالوا: بل بنفسِ وجودِها تنعدمُ، ولا بقاء لها أصلاً، وسواء ما شُوهِدَ فيهِ ذلكَ؛ كالحركاتِ والأصوات، أو لا؛ كالألوان والاعتقادات (1). قالوا: لأنَّها لو بقيَتْ لاستحال عدمُها؛ لما ذُكِرَ في التقسيم، فألزموا مثل ذلك في الجواهر مع أنَّها تبقى ويصح عدمُها، فأجابوا بأنَّ شرط بقائها إمدادها بالأعراض، فإذا أراد الله إعدامها قطع عنها خلق الأعراض.
Know that by a similar proof, the Imams of Ahl al-Sunna (may God be pleased with them) argued for the impossibility of accidents enduring. They said: Rather, by their very existence they cease to exist, and they have no endurance at all, whether they are such whose cessation is observed, like movements and sounds, or not, like colors and beliefs. They said: Because if they endured, their non-existence would be impossible, due to what was mentioned in the division. So they required the same for substances (jawahir) despite the fact that they endure and their non-existence is possible. They answered that the condition for their enduring is the bestowal of accidents upon them, so when God wills to annihilate them, He cuts off the creation of accidents.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage presents the Ash'ari proof that accidents (a'rad) do not endure (istihalat baqa' al-a'rad). The proof is analogous to the earlier one for God's eternal continuance: if accidents endured, they could not cease, but they are observed to cease, so they do not endure. The objection is raised that substances (jawahir) endure yet can cease, so why can't accidents? The answer is that substances endure only because God continuously creates accidents in them; when He stops creating, the substance ceases. Thus, accidents are created anew each instant and have no endurance.

Key Terms
أعراض
استحالة بقاء الأعراض
جوهر
إمداد الأعراض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think accidents could endure like substances; the Ash'ari view is they are constantly re-created.
Correction: Accidents do not endure at all; they are created anew each instant. Substances only appear to endure because God continuously creates accidents in them.

Checkpoint
According to the Imams, what is the condition for substances to endure?
A) they are self-subsistent
B) bestowal of accidents upon them
C) God's direct preservation without accidents
D) their own nature

Key Takeaway
Accidents do not endure; they are created anew each instant, and substances endure only because God continuously creates accidents in them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Ash'ari proof shows that your very thoughts and beliefs are accidents that do not endure—they are recreated each moment by God. If you were to examine your current belief in God, would you find it to be a genuine conviction sustained by God, or a mere habit that you assume persists on its own? What will you do today to ensure that your faith is actively renewed by God's creation?
?
Consider that even the color you see right now is an accident that does not last; it is a fresh creation from God. When you look at your own hands, do you sense the immediate presence of God's creative act? How would your experience of the world change if you paused every hour to acknowledge that everything you perceive is being recreated by God at that very moment?
?
The passage says that when God wills to destroy a substance, He merely stops creating accidents in it. If God did not sustain you for even a single instant, you would cease to exist. Are you living as if your existence and your abilities are self-sufficient? Spend a few minutes now to silently thank God for each moment of existence, and commit to one action today that demonstrates your total dependence on Him.

Two Proofs for the Necessity of a Preponderant
Sanusi presents two proofs for the necessity of a preponderant for the contingent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two arguments Sanusi uses to prove that a contingent being requires a preponderant (murajjih) to bring it into existence.

Core Idea
Contingent existence always demands a preponderant; without it, logical and ontological absurdities follow.

Sanusi now presents two tightly packed arguments that establish a foundational principle of Ash'ari theology: every contingent being requires a preponderant cause. The first argument appeals to the impossibility of an effect being delayed from its cause. The second, more complex argument, considers the scenario of the opposite (non-existence) and shows that only a preponderant can resolve the dilemma. Let's work through these arguments carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Allow the author's own argumentative structure to come through before interpreting.
Notice that the passage uses 'also' (أيضاً) to introduce each proof.
2
Identify the first proof
The first proof is brief: it states the impossibility of the delay of the effect (athar) from its cause (muqtadi). Ask yourself: why is this delay impossible? Because it would mean the cause exists but its effect does not, which contradicts the definition of causality.
This proof relies on a basic ontological principle.
3
Understand the second proof
The second proof is more involved. It considers the opposite (al-didd), i.e., the non-existence of the contingent. Under the assumption of no preponderant, the opposite would either be preponderated over the existence (tarjih al-marjuh) or equal to it (musawi). Sanusi then gives a reason why defending the prior existence (the eternal) is more appropriate, and then presents a dilemma about the opposite subsisting in the eternal.
Break the second proof into its sub-arguments: the principle of defending prior existence, and the impossibility of coexistence of opposites.
4
Connect to the conclusion
Both proofs lead to the same conclusion: the contingent must have a preponderant that specifies its existence over non-existence. Without it, absurd consequences follow.
This conclusion is a cornerstone of the Ash'ari proof for the existence of God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لاستحالة تأخر المقتضي عن أثره، وأيضاً يلزم في الضد ترجيح المرجوح، ولا أقل من المساوي؛ إذ دفع القديم السابق وجوده لطريان ضده أولى من العكس، وأيضاً فالضد إن قام بالقديم لزم اجتماع الضدين، وإلا بطل اقتضاؤه؛ لعدم الاختصاص
Because of the impossibility of the delay of the effect from its cause; also, there would be in the opposite preponderance of the inferior, or at least equality; for repelling the pre-existent [eternal] whose existence preceded [the occurrence of] its opposite is more appropriate than the reverse; also, if the opposite subsisted in the pre-existent, then the conjunction of two opposites would be necessary; otherwise, its being an effect would be invalid because of lack of specification.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage presents two proofs for the necessity of a preponderant (murajjih) for the contingent (hadith) to come into existence. The first proof: It is impossible for the effect (athar) to be delayed from its cause (muqtadi). If the contingent could exist without a preponderant, then its effect would be delayed, which is impossible. The second proof: In the case of the opposite (al-didd), namely the non-existence of the contingent, there would be a preponderance of the inferior (tarjih al-marjuh) over the superior, or at least equality. This is because defending the eternal (qadim) whose existence preceded the occurrence of its opposite (i.e., preventing the opposite from occurring) is more appropriate than the reverse (defending the non-existence). If the opposite (the contingent's non-existence) were to subsist in the eternal, then two opposites would coexist in it, which is impossible. Otherwise, its being an effect would be invalid due to lack of specification (ikhtisas). Thus the contingent must have a preponderant that specifies its existence.

Key Terms
مقتضي
أثر
ضد
ترجيح المرجوح
مساوي
قديم
اقتضاء
اختصاص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the second argument is merely about logical consistency, without recognizing the ontological principle that defending the prior existence is more appropriate.
Correction: The argument relies on the Ash'ari principle that defending the eternal (which already exists) is more appropriate than defending the non-existent opposite. This is not just logical but ontological.

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the consequence if the opposite (non-existence) were to subsist in the eternal?
A) The eternal would cease to exist.
B) Two opposites would coexist in one subject.
C) The contingent would be eternal.
D) The effect would be delayed.

Key Takeaway
The contingent being cannot exist without a preponderant; otherwise, absurd consequences such as delay of effect or coexistence of opposites would follow.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that your existence at every moment requires a Preponderant (Allah), how would that change your sense of dependence on Him? Are there areas where you still act as if you are self-sufficient? What would it look like to live in constant awareness that you are sustained moment by moment?
?
The argument shows that without a preponderant, absurdity follows. Reflect on a time when you relied on something other than God to give you stability—did it lead to inner contradiction or a sense of being unsupported? How does this argument invite you to put your trust solely in the Eternal?
?
Sanusi states that 'repelling the pre-existent is more appropriate'—defending what has always been is more fitting. In your spiritual life, do you give priority to what is eternal (God's commands) over what is temporary? What does it mean to 'defend' the priority of the eternal in your daily decisions and habits?

Ash'ari Debate on Accident Persistence: Al-Razi vs. Early Ash'aris
Sanusi contrasts al-Razi and early Ash'aris on accident persistence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the early Ash'ari argument against the persistence of accidents and how it differs from al-Razi's position.

Core Idea
Accident persistence debates hinge on whether a meaning can inhere in a meaning.

This passage presents a key disagreement within the Ash'ari school regarding whether accidents (a'rad) can persist over time. The early Ash'aris argued that persistence requires a separate attribute (al-baqa'), which would lead to an impossible 'meaning inhering in a meaning'. Fakhr al-Din al-Razi rejected this reasoning. Let's examine the argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem of preponderator
Note the opening sentence about the preponderator (al-murajjih) and its role in making a possible thing occur. This sets up the difficulty about accident persistence.
This part is a brief reference; focus on the core argument.
2
Contrast the two positions
The passage mentions that al-Razi affirmed accident persistence, while early Ash'aris denied it. Understand why each side held its view.
3
Analyze the early Ash'ari proof
Early Ash'aris believed that persisting things require a state of remaining (al-baqa') that inheres in them. If accidents persisted, this state of remaining (itself an accident) would inhere in an accident, which they deemed impossible because it would be 'a meaning inhering in a meaning'.
4
Connect to broader theology
The doctrine that accidents cannot persist has significant implications for understanding the nature of the world and divine action. Reflect on how this argument shapes Ash'ari occasionalism.
The passage ends by stating the correct view has been already given earlier.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرجح ، واللاحق طارى ، ومقتضاه ترجيح طرف الممكنِ وترجيح الممكن لا يستغني عن المؤثر ، فلأجل هذا تردَّدَ في بقاء الأعراض . وجزم الفخرُ في «المعالم » بصحة بقائها(۱) ، وقدماء الأشعريَّةِ لمَّا اعتقدوا أنَّ الباقي باقٍ ببقاء ، وأنَّ الجواهرَ إِنَّما صح بقاؤُها لقيامِ البقاء بها . . قالوا : لو بقيت الأعراضُ لزمَ قيام المعنى بالمعنى ، وهو محال . ، وقد تقدَّمَ أنَّ التحقيق في البقاء خلافُهُ (۲)
The preponderant and the subsequent accidental [i.e., the preponderator and the accident] – its requirement is to preponderate one of the two possible sides, and preponderating the possible is not independent of an effect. For this reason, there was doubt about the persistence of accidents. Fakhr al-Din [al-Razi] affirmed in 'al-Ma'alim' the validity of their persistence. And when the early Ash'aris believed that what remains remains through a state of remaining, and that substances are only validly persistent due to the subsistence of the state of remaining in them, they said: 'If accidents persisted, it would entail a meaning inhering in a meaning, which is impossible.' And it has preceded that the correct investigation regarding persistence is contrary to that.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage presents a theological argument regarding the persistence (بقاء) of accidents (الأعراض). It begins by referring to a previous discussion about the 'preponderator' (المرجح) and the 'subsequent accidental' (اللاحق طارى), stating that the requirement of the preponderator is to preponderate one of the two possible sides, and that preponderating a possible thing cannot be independent of an effect (مؤثر). This difficulty leads to doubt about whether accidents persist. The passage then notes that Fakhr al-Din al-Razi (الفخر) affirmed in his work 'al-Ma'alim' that accidents do persist. In contrast, the early Ash'aris (قدماء الأشعرية) held a different view. They believed that a persisting thing (الباقي) remains through a state of remaining (بقاء), and that substances (الجواهر) only persist because the state of remaining subsists in them. Based on this, they argued: if accidents persisted, it would necessitate a meaning (المعنى) inhering in another meaning – i.e., the accident of remaining inhering in the accident itself – which they considered impossible. The sentence ends by stating that the correct view has already been presented earlier, which is contrary to the early Ash'ari position.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the Ash'ari position on accident persistence is uniform.
Correction: This passage shows that the early Ash'aris opposed accident persistence, while later figures like al-Razi affirmed it.

Checkpoint
Why did the early Ash'aris argue that accidents cannot persist?
A) Because accidents are temporally originated and thus cannot persist.
B) Because the persistence of an accident would require a meaning (the accident of remaining) inhering in another meaning (the accident itself), which is impossible.
C) Because accidents are not real entities.
D) Because substances alone have the capacity to persist.

Key Takeaway
The early Ash'ari argument against accident persistence rests on the principle that a meaning cannot inhere in another meaning, a claim later Ash'is like al-Razi rejected.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If accidents like health, wealth, and even your own existence do not persist by themselves but require a state of remaining from Allah, how does that change your daily reliance on Him? Choose one thing you consider stable and ask yourself: Do I act as if it persists on its own, or do I consciously attribute its continuation to Allah? What would change if you truly believed it could vanish at any moment?
?
The early Ash'aris argued that a meaning cannot inhere in another meaning—no created thing can carry another's persistence. Where in your life do you treat secondary causes (your job, your family, your knowledge) as if they have independent power to sustain themselves or you? How can this lesson push you toward a deeper tawakkul, trusting only Allah for persistence?

Two Ways to Falsify the Necessary Consequence
Sanusi enumerates two ways to falsify the opponent's necessary consequence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two methods by which Sanusi demonstrates that an opponent's necessary consequence (lāzim) is false, and how these methods rely on the observed specificity in contingent things and the impossibility of a contingent being eternally non-existent.

Core Idea
A contingent cannot be left unspecified—either its existence or non-existence demands a specifier.

Sanusi continues his discussion of rational judgments by explaining how to falsify an opponent's claim of a necessary consequence. He presents two distinct approaches: one based on the direct observation of specificity in the world, and another based on the logical impossibility of a contingent being either eternal or perpetually non-existent. Both lead to the same conclusion: the necessity of a specifying agent, which is Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the full Arabic text once without analysis. Let the structure of Sanusi's argument sink in.
Notice the two 'ways' are introduced with 'فبوجهين'.
2
Identify the two ways
Identify the first way (observation of specificity) and the second way (logical dilemma). Note how Sanusi states the two alternatives.
The second way is elaborated further, while the first is stated briefly.
3
Understand the second way's reasoning
Follow the explanation of why the absence of specificity leads to either eternity or perpetual non-existence, and why both are impossible.
Sanusi uses the proof of temporal origination and empirical observation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأمَّا بطلان اللازم فبوجهين :
أحدهما : مشاهدة الاختصاص في الممكناتِ
والثاني : وهو ما أشار إليهِ في العقيدة مِنْ لزوم اتصافِ ذاتِ الممكن بأحد أمرين : وجوب القدم ، أو استمرار العدمِ ، وكلاهما محال فى حقِّهِ ؛ أمَّا الأَوَّلُ : فلِمَا مضى مِنْ برهان حدوثِ الممكناتِ كلها ، وأما الثاني : فلمشاهدة الوجودِ فيها
وبيانُ لزومِ أحدِ الأمرين عند تقدير عدم الاختصاص بممكن دونَ ممكن : أنَّ عدم الاختصاص بـالـوجـود وما يتبعُهُ مِنَ المقدارِ المخصوص والصفة المخصوصة .. يُوجِبُ استمرار العدم ، وعدم الاختصاص بالزمن المعيَّنِ . . يُوجِبُ القدمَ أو استمرار العدم ؛ لأنَّ الزمنَ لمَّا كانَ لا يَتَصفُ  ِبهِ إلا المتجدِّدُ .. فلا ينتفي عنه إلا القديم أو المستمر العدم ؛ إذْ لا تجدُّدَ لهما ، فظهر أنَّ لزوم الاتصاف بأحد عند الأمرينِ عدم الاختصاص بتلك الأمور المذكورة.. يتعيَّنُ أحدهما ؛ وهو استمرار العدم فيما عدا الزمان ، ويلزم أحدهما لا بعينه في الزمانِ ، لكن لم يُفصِّلْ في العقيدة ؛ لأنَّه قصد ما يلزم في عدم الكلِّ مِنْ حيثُ هو كلٌّ ، لا ما يلزم في عدم كلّ واحد
As for the falsity of the necessary consequence, it is in two ways: One of them: observation of specificity in contingent things. The second: which is what he indicated in al-Aqida from the necessity of the contingent's essence being characterized by one of two matters: necessity of eternity, or perpetual non-existence, both impossible with respect to it. As for the first: for what preceded from the proof of the temporal origination of all contingents. And as for the second: for the observation of existence in them. And the explanation of the necessity of one of the two matters when assuming the absence of specificity for one contingent over another: that the absence of specificity in existence and what follows it of specific quantity and specific quality... necessitates perpetual non-existence, and the absence of specificity in the specified time... necessitates eternity or perpetual non-existence; because time is only characterized by what is temporal... so only the eternal or perpetually non-existent are negated from it, since there is no temporality for them. So it appears that the necessity of being characterized by one of the two matters when there is absence of specificity in those mentioned matters... one of them is determined, which is perpetual non-existence in other than time, and one of them is necessitated but not specific in time. But he did not detail in al-Aqida because he intended what is necessary from the absence of the whole as a whole, not what is necessary from the absence of each individual.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage enumerates two ways to falsify the necessary consequence (بطلان اللازم) of an opponent's argument. The first way is the observed specificity (مشاهدة الاختصاص) in contingent things—we see that contingent things are distinguished from each other by specific qualities, quantities, and times, implying a specifying agent. The second way is the argument from the definition of a contingent: its essence cannot be left without either being eternal or never existing, both impossible. The impossibility of eternity is already proven by the demonstration of the temporal origination (برهان حدوث الممكنات) of all contingents. The impossibility of perpetual non-existence is refuted by the observation that contingent beings do exist (مشاهدة الوجود). Sanusi then elaborates on the second way: if there were no specificity (اختصاص) assigning existence, quantity, quality, or a particular time to a contingent, then that contingent would either be eternal (if no time is specified) or would never exist (if no existence is specified). Since both are impossible, specificity must exist. He notes that the creed (العقيدة) did not distinguish between the two cases because it treats the absence of all forms of specificity collectively.

Key Terms
بطلان اللازم
اختصاص
وجوب القدم
استمرار العدم
برهان حدوث الممكنات
مشاهدة الوجود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the impossibility of both eternity and perpetual non-existence is argued from the same proof.
Correction: Sanusi distinguishes: the impossibility of eternity is from the proof of temporal origination, while the impossibility of perpetual non-existence is from observed existence.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi's second way, what are the two impossible alternatives that a contingent's essence would have to be characterized by if there were no specificity?
A) Necessity of existence and impossibility of non-existence
B) Necessity of eternity and perpetual non-existence
C) Temporal origination and spatial limitation
D) Possibility and actuality

Key Takeaway
Sanusi shows that an opponent's necessary consequence can be falsified either by empirical observation of specificity in contingent things or by logical deduction that a contingent cannot lack a specifier.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you observe the specific details of your existence—your birthplace, time, abilities—do you truly see the hand of a Specifier, or do you take these as meaningless chance? What would change in your gratitude right now if you believed each detail was chosen for you by Allah?
?
If your very existence depends on Allah's specific will, how does this affect the way you use the time He has specified for you? Is there a specific moment today you have been wasting that you will now use for His sake?
?
Sanusi argues that without a specifier, a contingent cannot exist at all. Your existence is proof that Allah chose you to be. What does that choice demand from you in return? What will you do today to live in a way that honors that choice?

Proof that the Maker Must Be an Agent by Choice
Sanusi proves the Maker must act by choice using a dilemma argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's proof that the Maker of the world cannot be a nature or cause but must act by choice, and why the two alternatives lead to impossible consequences.

Core Idea
If the Maker were a nature or cause, the world would be either eternal or impossible — both false.

Sanusi now turns to establish not just that the Maker exists, but how He acts. He argues that the Maker cannot be a blind nature or necessary cause, because that would force the world to be either eternal or non-existent. Instead, the Maker must be an agent who acts by will and choice. The following passage presents a concise dilemma that rules out all alternatives.

Guided Path
1
Understand the dilemma
Recognize that Sanusi presents two and only two possibilities for the Maker being a nature or cause: it must be either eternal (qadim) or originated (hadith).
This is a standard kalam technique: exhaust the possibilities.
2
Trace the consequences of each branch
Follow the reasoning: if eternal, the world must be eternal (since nature/cause acts by necessity, not choice); if originated, it leads to circularity or infinite regress.
Both consequences are already proven false: the world is temporal, and circularity/regress are impossible.
3
Draw the conclusion
Since both branches are impossible, the original assumption is false. Therefore, the Maker must be an agent by choice (fa'il bi al-ikhtiyar).
The Quranic verse confirms this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبيانُ لزوم أحدِ الأمرينِ إِذا قُدَّرَ صانعُ العالم طبيعةً أو عِلَّةً : أَنَّ الطبيعة والعلَّةَ لا يخلو أن تكونا قديمتين أو حادثتين ، فإن كانتا قديمتين لزم قدمُ العالم ؛ لأنَّ فعل العلة والطبيعة إنَّما هو باللزوم لا بالاختيار، وقدمُ الملزوم يقضي بقدم لازمه ، وقد عرفت بالبرهان حدوث العالم ، وإن كانتا حادثتينِ افتقرتا إلى عِلَّةٍ أو طبيعة ، ودارَ أو تسلسل ، وقد سبق بيان ذلكَ عندَ بيان كون فاعلكَ قديماً ، والدورُ والتسلسل محالانِ على ما مضى ، فكونُ العلة والطبيعة حادثتين محال ، فوجود ذاتِكَ وسائرِ العالم الموقوفِ عليهما محال ، والمحالُ مستمر العدمِ ، فقد لزم استمرار العدمِ لذاتِكَ ولسائر العالم ! والعِيانُ يُكَذِّبُ ذلك. والحاصلُ : أَنَّهُ يلزمُ قدمُ العالمِ إِنْ فُرِضَتِ العَلَّةُ أَوِ الطبيعةُ قديمتين ، واستمرار عدمِهِ إِنْ فُرضتا حادثتين ، وكلا اللازمين باطل فالملزوم - وهو كون صانع العالم طبيعة أو عِلَّة - باطل ، فتعيَّنَ أَنْ يكون فاعلاً بالاختيار ، وهو المطلوب ، وَرَبُّكَ يَخْلُقُ مَا يَشَاءُ ويختارُ [القصص : ٦٨] .
And the explanation of the necessity of one of two matters when the Maker of the world is assumed to be a nature or a cause: that the nature and the cause are not free from being either eternal or originated. If they are eternal, the eternity of the world follows, because the action of the cause and nature is only by necessary consequence (luzum) not by choice, and the eternity of the substrate requires the eternity of its necessary concomitant. And you have known by proof the temporality of the world. And if they are originated, they would need a cause or a nature, leading to circularity or infinite regress. And this has been previously explained in the discussion of your Maker being eternal. Circularity and infinite regress are impossible as has passed. So the nature and cause being originated is impossible. So the existence of your essence and the rest of the world that depend on them is impossible. And the impossible is perpetually non-existent. So the perpetual non-existence of your essence and the rest of the world would follow! But direct observation contradicts that. The conclusion: that the eternity of the world follows if the cause or nature is assumed eternal, and its perpetual non-existence follows if they are assumed originated. Both consequences are false, so the premise—that the Maker of the world is a nature or a cause—is false. So it is determined that He must be an agent by choice, and that is what is sought. 'And your Lord creates what He wills and chooses' [Qasas:68].
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage is a proof (dalil) that the Maker of the world is an agent by choice (fa'il bi al-ikhtiyar), not a nature (tabi') or a cause ('illa). The author begins by stating the two possibilities for the nature or cause: they must be either eternal (qadim) or originated (hadith). He then shows that both possibilities lead to absurdities. If eternal, then the world must be eternal because the action of a cause or nature is by necessary logical consequence (bil-luzum), not by choice; since the cause is eternal, its effect must also be eternal. But we have already proven the world's temporality. If originated, then they would themselves require a cause or nature, leading either to circularity (dawr) or infinite regress (tasalsul), both of which have been shown to be impossible. Therefore, it is impossible for the Maker to be a nature or a cause. The author then concludes that the opposite must be true: the Maker is an agent by choice, citing the Quranic verse. This argument is a classic demonstration of the necessity of divine choice (ikhtiyar).

Key Terms
طبيعة (nature)
علة (cause)
فاعل بالاختيار (agent by choice)
لزوم (necessary consequence)
قدم (eternality)
حدوث (temporality)
دور (circularity)
تسلسل (infinite regress)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if the cause is eternal, its effect must also be eternal only if the cause is voluntary; they miss that the issue is the mode of agency (necessary vs. voluntary).
Correction: The argument relies on the fact that a nature or cause acts by necessity (luzum), not choice, so eternality of cause necessitates eternality of effect regardless of volition.

Checkpoint
What are the two possibilities for a nature or cause assumed as the Maker of the world, and what impossible consequences follow from each?
A) Eternal leads to world's eternity; originated leads to infinite regress/circularity.
B) Eternal leads to world's nonexistence; originated leads to world's eternity.
C) Both lead to the world's temporality.
D) Both lead to the world's eternity.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi's dilemma shows that the Maker cannot be a nature or cause, because that would force the world to be either eternal or impossible; therefore, the Maker must be an agent who acts by choice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live as though your Lord creates what He wills and chooses, or do you sometimes act as if your circumstances are forced by natural causes beyond His control? What would change in your daily reliance on Him if you fully internalized this argument?
?
The proof shows that your very existence depends on a deliberate act of God's choice. Are you living in gratitude for that election, or do you take your existence for granted? What one habit can you adopt to remind yourself that your life is a direct result of His will?
?
If God were a blind cause, your life would either be eternal or impossible—yet you are here, mortal and contingent. How does this urgent reality call you to surrender your own plans to His choice? What are you holding onto today that you need to entrust to His will and choice?

The Impossibility of an Actual Infinite
Sanusi argues that an eternal cause entails an actual infinite, which is impossible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why assuming an eternal cause or nature leads to the impossible consequence of an actual infinite number of coexisting possible things.

Core Idea
A co-eternal cause would produce all possible things at once — an actual infinite.

Sanusi presents a final devastating consequence for those who posit an eternal cause or nature alongside Allah. If such a cause existed, its relation to all possible effects would be equal, meaning it would produce every possible thing simultaneously, resulting in an actual infinite number of coexisting entities. This impossibility, he notes, afflicts not only the eternal cause hypothesis but also the assumption of an originated cause, strengthening the overall refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the core argument. Then read it a second time, tracing how each premise leads to the conclusion.
The argument is compact: assumption → same relation → all possibles at once → impossible.
2
Identify key concepts
Find the terms for 'infinity', 'possible things', and 'simultaneously' in Arabic and English. Understand how they connect.
3
Understand the logical chain
Map the argument: if the cause is eternal, its relation to all possible effects is identical (one and the same). Therefore, all possible effects must exist at once, producing an actual infinite. This is deemed impossible.
The kalam principle that an actual infinite cannot exist is at work here.
4
Note the twist
The author adds that this impossibility also holds if the cause is originated. Why? Because the relation to all possibles is still one and the same always. This broadens the refutation.
This shows the argument is not limited to the eternal cause assumption.
5
Reflect on the principle
Consider why an actual infinite coexisting reality is impossible in kalam. This underpins many arguments for the necessary existence of a single Creator.
Contrast with modern mathematical infinities, which are potential or conceptual, not actual.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويلزم أيضاً على تقديرِ العلَّةِ أو الطبيعة قديمتين وجود ما لا نهاية له ؛ لأنَّ نسبة العلّة والطبيعة إلى الممكنات نسبة واحدة ، والممكناتُ لا نهاية لها ، فيلزم وجود جميعها دفعةً ، وهذا المحالُ في الحقيقة لا يختص لزومُهُ بفَرْضِ قدم العلَّةِ أو الطبيعة ، بل يلزم أيضاً في فرض حدوثهما .
And it also follows on the assumption of the cause or nature being eternal the existence of what has no end (infinity); because the relation of the cause and nature to the possible things is one and the same relation, and the possible things have no end, so the existence of all of them at once follows. And this impossibility in reality is not specific to the assumption of the eternity of the cause or nature, but it also follows on the assumption of their origination.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage is a corollary to the previous argument. The author points out that if the cause or nature were eternal, then its relation to all possible effects is equal, meaning it would produce all possible things simultaneously, resulting in an infinite number of existents. This is impossible. Interestingly, he notes that this same impossibility also holds even if the cause or nature were originated, because the relation to all possibilities is still one and the same. Thus, the absurdity of an infinite simultaneous existence undermines both possibilities, strengthening the overall refutation of the nature/cause hypothesis.

دفعة

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many assume an actual infinite can exist in reality (e.g., an infinite number of coexisting things).
Correction: The author argues that an actual infinite number of coexisting things is impossible, a key kalam principle derived from the impossibility of a simultaneous infinite.

Checkpoint

C) The cause produces only one effect at a time.
D) The relation depends on the will of the agent.

Key Takeaway
Assuming an eternal cause forces an actual infinite of coexistent possibles, which is impossible — and the same problem arises even if the cause is created.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
You cannot avoid the force of this logic: an actual infinite is impossible. If you truly accept that, what created thing are you holding onto as if it were infinite or independent? Will you let go of that false security today?

Juwayni's Critique of the Design Argument
Sanusi reports Juwayni's weakening of the design argument and the start of an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam al-Haramayn's (al-Juwayni's) weakening of the classical argument from design (dalalat al-ihkam) and the beginning of Ibn al-Tilimsani's objection.

Core Idea
Juwayni argues that precision (ihkam) is mere spatial arrangement, insufficient to prove God's knowledge directly.

In kalam, the argument from design (dalalat al-ihkam) was a key proof for God's knowledge. However, even classical scholars critically examined its foundations. Here, Sanusi reports Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni's attempt to weaken this argument by redefining what 'precision' means, and the initial response by Sharaf al-Din ibn al-Tilimsani. This passage shows the sophisticated internal debates within Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Note that the objection is incomplete.
The passage ends mid-sentence; don't expect a full resolution.
2
Understand Juwayni's definition of precision
Juwayni defines 'ihkam' narrowly: it is simply accidents specifying substances with places, producing straight lines. Why does he think this does not indicate knowledge directly?
3
Identify his positive argument
Juwayni says the real discussion presupposes a free agent (mukhtar), and free choice itself implies knowledge. Notice the shift from design to free agency.
4
Consider Ibn al-Tilimsani's objection
The objection begins: 'that precision is not granted'. What might he be contesting? Think about what could be challenged in Juwayni's reduction.
The objection is incomplete, so we only have a hint.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد ضعف إمام الحرمين في البرهان » دلالة الإحكام على العلم وقال : ( لا معنى للإحكام سوى أنَّ الأكوانَ حَصَّصَتِ الجواهر بأحياز (١) حتى انتظم منها خطوط مستقيمة (۱)، ولا اختصاص للأكوانِ بالدلالةِ على العلم، وإِنَّما الكلامُ معَ الخصم بعد كونه صانعاً مختاراً، والاختيار دليل كونِهِ عالماً ((۲) واعترض عليه شرفُ الدين بنُ التَّلمساني بأنَّ الإحكام لا تُسلم
And Imam al-Haramayn weakened in al-Burhan the indication of precision (ihkam) upon knowledge and said: 'There is no meaning of precision except that the accidents (akwan) specified the substances (jawahir) with places (ahiyaz) until straight lines were arranged from them, and there is no special property of the accidents in indicating knowledge; rather the discussion with the opponent is after his being a free agent (maker), and free choice is a proof of his being knowledgeable.' And Sharf al-Din ibn al-Tilimsani objected to him that precision is not granted...
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage presents a theological debate on the argument from design (dalalat al-ihkam 'ala al-ilm). Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni) weakened this argument by offering a narrow definition of 'ihkam' (precision): he says it merely consists of the accidents (akwan, i.e., spatial configurations) specifying the substances (jawahir) with particular places (ahiyaz), which results in straight lines. According to him, such accidents have no special capacity to indicate knowledge; the real argument must presuppose that the maker is a free agent (mukhtar), and then free choice itself implies knowledge. This seems to reduce the classical design argument. Then Sharf al-Din ibn al-Tilimsani objects, 'that precision is not granted', but his objection is cut off. The fragment suggests he disagrees that precision can be reduced to mere spatial specification. The passage thus shows a sophisticated kalam discussion on the validity of the teleological argument.

أحياز

اختيار
دليل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument from design is so obvious that no scholar ever questioned it.
Correction: This passage shows that a major kalam scholar (Juwayni) critically analyzed and weakened the design argument, and his student Ibn al-Tilimsani objected.

Checkpoint

B) The specification of substances by accidents with places, resulting in straight lines
C) The purposeful order in the universe
D) The knowledge of the maker

Key Takeaway
Juwayni redefined the design argument to focus on free agency rather than cosmic order, showing that even foundational proofs were subject to rigorous scrutiny.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Juwayni argues that merely observing order in the universe does not itself prove God's knowledge; rather, you must first recognize your own free agency. When have you assumed that physical evidence alone is enough to sustain your faith, without deeply connecting it to your personal choices and accountability to a knowing Creator? What would it change in your daily life if you truly saw every decision you make as a response to an all-knowing God?
?
The passage shows Juwayni questioning even a widely accepted proof. Are there beliefs about God that you hold simply because 'everyone says so'—including your own understanding of your faith? What one conviction are you willing to reexamine honestly, not to doubt it, but to own it personally as Juwayni did?
?
Juwayni shifts the argument from external precision to internal free agency. Think of a recent moment when you made a conscious choice. Did you act as if God's knowledge was present in that decision, or did you behave as if it were insignificant? How would your attitude toward that choice change if you remembered that your ability to choose is itself a proof of God's knowledge, demanding gratitude and responsibility?
